<p><i><b>FutureSex/LoveSounds</b></i> is the second studio album by American singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>. It was released on September 8, 2006 by <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> and its affiliated label of the <a href="/wiki/Zomba_Group_of_Companies" title="Zomba Group of Companies">Zomba Group of Companies</a>. During a two-year hiatus, Timberlake resolved his feelings on being unable to record any new material, and as he returned to record some new music, he began collaborating with his longtime <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record producer</a> <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, alongside the latter's colleague <a href="/wiki/Danja_(record_producer)" title="Danja (record producer)">Danja</a>. The album's contents were produced at Timbaland's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Crown_Studios" title="Thomas Crown Studios">Thomas Crown Studios</a>. The album shares some lyrical themes with Timberlake's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Justified_(album)" title="Justified (album)">Justified</a></i> (2002), although <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> has more diversity in music genres. It infuses <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> with <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a>, and elements of <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Reprise" title="Reprise">reprises</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(music)" title="Bridge (music)">interludes</a> interspersed on the album's tracks were created by the production team with the goal of channeling Timberlake's influences; including <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>.</p>
<p><i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> received mostly positive reviews from critics, who noted its wide range of influences and collection of eclectic sounds. The album produced six singles that attained chart success; including U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> number-one singles: "<a href="/wiki/SexyBack" title="SexyBack">SexyBack</a>", "<a href="/wiki/My_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="My Love (Justin Timberlake song)">My Love</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_Around..._Comes_Around" title="What Goes Around... Comes Around">What Goes Around... Comes Around</a>". With "<a href="/wiki/Summer_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Summer Love (Justin Timberlake song)">Summer Love</a>", the album achieved four U.S. <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40" title="Mainstream Top 40">Mainstream Top 40</a> number-one songs. <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine ranked the album at number 46 on its list of the best albums of the 2000s, and aside from earning numerous best-of-the-decade lists, the album received several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/49th_Grammy_Awards" title="49th Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a> nominations; including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a>. It has been <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">certified multi-platinum</a> in many countries worldwide, and has sold over ten million copies, with four million in the United States. The album has been added to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>'s musical library and archive.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JustinTimberlake.jpg"><img alt="A young man dressed in black shirt and pants is walking while holding a golf stick" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2263" data-file-width="1309" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/JustinTimberlake.jpg/150px-JustinTimberlake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/JustinTimberlake.jpg/225px-JustinTimberlake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/JustinTimberlake.jpg/300px-JustinTimberlake.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JustinTimberlake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Timberlake in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In November 2002, Justin Timberlake released his debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Justified_(album)" title="Justified (album)">Justified</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> and produced the US top-five singles: "<a href="/wiki/Rock_Your_Body" title="Rock Your Body">Rock Your Body</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Cry_Me_a_River_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Cry Me a River (Justin Timberlake song)">Cry Me a River</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> "Cry Me a River" in particular was credited for having helped the album sell and peak on the music charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup> <i>Justified</i> ended selling four million copies in the United States alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup> Although the album established Timberlake's career outside his then-band <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%27NSYNC" title="'NSYNC">*NSYNC</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burnt_out_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-burnt_out-4">[4]</a></sup> Timberlake (who was 22 years old at the time), was "at a crossroads" and felt he was at the stage of being "burnt out",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvnews1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvnews1-5">[5]</a></sup> and thought he had lost his voice "in regards to knowing what (and how) he wanted to sing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvnews1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvnews1-5">[5]</a></sup> Timberlake stated that <i>Justified</i> had been years in the making, and a record that would re-create its success would be a challenge he was not ready to take.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss2_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moss2-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the following years, Timberlake went partially idle in the music industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup> His being "burnt out" partly caused him to try acting in films. In October 2003, he hosted and was the guest musician on the late-night <a href="/wiki/Variety_show" title="Variety show">variety show</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, where he showcased his acting potentials. He also paired with American actor <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fallon" title="Jimmy Fallon">Jimmy Fallon</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Barry_Gibb_Talk_Show" title="The Barry Gibb Talk Show">The Barry Gibb Talk Show</a></i>. After the show, Timberlake was reportedly "inundated" with acting offers, which he readily accepted partly because he needed inspiration and did not want to pass up the opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moss-7">[7]</a></sup> Before returning to music, Timberlake shot four films; including <i><a href="/wiki/Edison_(film)" title="Edison (film)">Edison Force</a></i> (2005) and <i><a href="/wiki/Alpha_Dog" title="Alpha Dog">Alpha Dog</a></i> (2006).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup> Timberlake opted not to pursue the reunion with *NSYNC, which he considered after <i>Justified</i>. According to him, he was concerned with how they would reinvent their music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burnt_out_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-burnt_out-4">[4]</a></sup> In late 2004, Timberlake then contacted record producers <a href="/wiki/Rich_Harrison" title="Rich Harrison">Rich Harrison</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Rodney Jerkins</a>, who had produced songs for *NSYNC. Both producers were "impressed" by the live band-driven late-night shows Timberlake had participated in and wanted to incorporate this in his music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss6_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moss6-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording">Recording</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>We had no direction at all ... other than '<a href="/wiki/Cry_Me_a_River_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Cry Me a River (Justin Timberlake song)">Cry Me a River</a>,' and not in the sense of mimicking the track, but in how big the song was. There was no direction for how he wanted the song to sound, because there was no direction for how he wanted [<i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>] to sound.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"> —producer Danja speaking to <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard2-9">[9]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>In 2005, Timberlake felt inspired to record songs again. Motivated by the "sad state" of pop radio, he decided he needed to experiment with music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup> Reportedly, it was not until Timberlake turned to producer <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> "that he figured out the direction he wanted the record to take".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VineyardMTVFunk_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-VineyardMTVFunk-10">[10]</a></sup> In November 2005, Timberlake visited Timbaland's brand-new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Crown_Studios" title="Thomas Crown Studios">Thomas Crown Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">Virginia Beach, Virginia</a>, United States. Timbaland had previously collaborated with Timberlake, producing four tracks for <i>Justified</i> including "Cry Me a River".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moss-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Once in the studio, however, the team had no clear direction for the album as there were no concepts being discussed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard2_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard2-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HovaVibeStudio_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-HovaVibeStudio-11">[11]</a></sup> Aside from having "Cry Me a River" to draw from, they had no "game plan" and no working title for the new album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard2_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard2-9">[9]</a></sup> Timberlake thought that if he could make a record that would live up to <i>Justified</i>, he "would have".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvnews1_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-mtvnews1-5">[5]</a></sup> So he asked Timbaland if he could reproduce the likes of "Cry Me a River" by four or six times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rolling_stone_cover_story_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-rolling_stone_cover_story-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>While in the studio, Timbaland played on the stereo plenty of songs by American singer and musician <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a> for them to listen to. Early in their sessions, they reportedly were "fooling around" and "freestyling".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard2_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard2-9">[9]</a></sup> One night, Danja was playing a guitar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riff" title="Riff">riff</a> and caught the attention of Timberlake, who then started humming to the <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a> and later sung the lyrics. Timbaland, who was at their side, added drums onto the progressing sound. After an hour, with no lyrics written on paper, Timberlake recorded in the vocal booth a song that would become "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_Around..._Comes_Around" title="What Goes Around... Comes Around">What Goes Around... Comes Around</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard2_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard2-9">[9]</a></sup> Timberlake, having been teased by Timbaland, said to the latter: "Let's do something we would never do. Let's go far left and just see what happens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvnews1_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-mtvnews1-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Official production for <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> started in December 2005. When production began, <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> Chairman and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Weiss" title="Barry Weiss">Barry Weiss</a>, asked when the album would be completed, to which Timberlake replied that it could possibly take a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScaggs20063_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScaggs20063-12">[12]</a></sup> The title was not finalized until Jive Records gave Timberlake a deadline on finishing what would become <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> The collective thought the album is comparable with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s landmark record, <i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i>, dubbing their own as <i>FS/LS Thriller 2006</i>. Timberlake is a fan of Jackson and even <a href="/wiki/Name-dropping" title="Name-dropping">name-drops</a> the latter in the song "Chop Me Up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Timberlake, <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is like a "fashion editorial, <a href="/wiki/Yves_Saint_Laurent_(brand)" title="Yves Saint Laurent (brand)">YSL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gucci" title="Gucci">Gucci</a> suits, which goes with the sonics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> The album's artworks were shot by American fashion photographer <a href="/wiki/Terry_Richardson" title="Terry Richardson">Terry Richardson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> The cover features Timberlake stomping a <a href="/wiki/Disco_ball" title="Disco ball">disco ball</a> using his black pointy shoe.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg/220px-Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg/330px-Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d1/Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg/440px-Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Timbaland_Live_Lyon_2007_FutureSex-LiveShow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> guested on several dates on Timberlake's 2007 <a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveShow" title="FutureSex/LoveShow">FutureSex/LoveShow</a> worldwide concert tour. Timbaland, his protégé Danja, and Timberlake wrote and produced a majority of tracks that appeared on the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For his new project, Timberlake collaborated with only few producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> With no concrete plans, however, Timberlake's goal for the album was "'to capture moments' with a vivid, raw, off-the-cuff sound".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup> Timberlake, who included <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record production</a> in his repertoire, managed the recording sessions with no formula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> His sessions with Timbaland and Danja were described as free-flowing, and he referred to themselves in the process as "looking like [mad men], a mad scientist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>On his collaboration with Timbaland, Timberlake asserted that they "have a very interesting connection" in music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> In ten days, they composed at least eight to ten songs with the lyrics, melodies, and vocals all in place. In three weeks, after that transitional moment with "What Goes Around... Comes Around", the collective was able to produce songs like "<a href="/wiki/My_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="My Love (Justin Timberlake song)">My Love</a>", "<a href="/wiki/SexyBack" title="SexyBack">SexyBack</a>", and "Sexy Ladies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScaggs20065_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScaggs20065-17">[17]</a></sup> Unlike <i>Justified</i> which was recorded in six weeks, Timberlake said that <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> took one year to complete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sessions for the album also saw Timberlake collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>, the latter himself a member of the hip hop group <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>, whose 2003 single "<a href="/wiki/Where_Is_the_Love%3F" title="Where Is the Love?">Where Is the Love?</a>" Timberlake lent vocals to. For the production, they are credited as Jawbreakers, a production team of their own established during their collaboration for The Black Eyed Peas' album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> Four songs were produced with will.i.am,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss3_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-Moss3-13">[13]</a></sup> although only "Damn Girl" made it to the standard edition of the album.</p>
<p>Actor <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rock" title="Chris Rock">Chris Rock</a> recommended producer Rubin to Timberlake, who considered the idea and discussed it with Rubin when he saw him at a music festival in <a href="/wiki/Coachella,_California" title="Coachella, California">Coachella, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss2_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moss2-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> Timberlake went to singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond" title="Neil Diamond">Neil Diamond</a>'s studio, where Rubin played him some <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demos</a>, one of which was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballad_(music)" title="Ballad (music)">ballad</a> that would become "(Another Song) All Over Again". Timberlake suggested that the collaboration was meant to "do the anti-whatever-you-want-to-call-it that [Timbaland and] I came up with".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the production of <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>, Timberlake was interested in <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScaggs20064_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScaggs20064-18">[18]</a></sup> This inspiration was used in his approach in recording the songs, rather than in composing them. Timberlake reveals, "I wanted to sing the song like a rock and roll singer, not an R&amp;B singer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VineyardMTVFunk_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-VineyardMTVFunk-10">[10]</a></sup> On the influences he drew from, he said that if <i>Justified</i> was "characterized" by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is more like <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> Other influences include late <a href="/wiki/INXS" title="INXS">INXS</a>-frontman <a href="/wiki/Michael_Hutchence" title="Michael Hutchence">Michael Hutchence</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Byrne" title="David Byrne">David Byrne</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Strokes" title="The Strokes">The Strokes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScaggs20064_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScaggs20064-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Timberlake expressed interest in recording songs with rock influences, Timbaland was initially reluctant to pursue the idea because he was not accustomed to producing such music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> Nonetheless, he suggested that they could produce a handful, since they were afraid of alienating Timberlake's urban fan base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> Because of this concern, they produced several <a href="/wiki/Reprise" title="Reprise">reprises</a>, encores and <a href="/wiki/Prelude_(music)" title="Prelude (music)">preludes</a> with a rock influence, instead of full-length songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> As to the sound of <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>, "<a href="/wiki/My_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="My Love (Justin Timberlake song)">My Love</a>", the second song composed, steered the album's direction. Danja revealed that it "changed the whole album",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HovaVibeStudio_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-HovaVibeStudio-11">[11]</a></sup> and the energy derived from the song was sustained throughout the process. On his inspiration for the infusion of R&amp;B with <a href="/wiki/Trance_music" title="Trance music">trance</a> in the album, Danja remembers:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>I heard <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">dance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Techno" title="Techno">techno</a> and was always interested in it but didn't really know where to go. But I went to a club one night and saw that people were losing their mind to these dance tracks. It wasn't really that I wanted to mimic that sound. I just wanted to have that energy and have people going crazy. So I knew the fusion was putting R&amp;B with trance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HovaVibeStudio_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-HovaVibeStudio-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Unlike his previous record that was intended to focus on <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> <a href="/wiki/Genre" title="Genre">genres</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is less concentrated on one particular sound,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss2_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Moss2-6">[6]</a></sup> thus representing a wider range. Timberlake explains, "It's more broad as far as the styles I wanted to mix in to my own type of thing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss2_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Moss2-6">[6]</a></sup> A musically "complex" album, <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is a fusion of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">rap</a>, rock, <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">funk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_wave_music" title="New wave music">new wave</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> noted that the album's sound is a "sonic departure" from both *NSYNC and <i>Justified</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20071_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20071-19">[19]</a></sup> Although "What Goes Around" sounds similar to <i>Justified</i>, Timberlake admitted that it is the only song in the new album to have such similarity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> Critics noted that the influences and styles are varied across the album's track list. The title track "<a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveSound" title="FutureSex/LoveSound">FutureSex/LoveSound</a>" incorporates early 1980s <a href="/wiki/New_wave_music" title="New wave music">new wave</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_rock" title="Industrial rock">industrial rock</a>. The song "Sexy Ladies" takes on <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis_sound" title="Minneapolis sound">Minneapolis funk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Another funk song on the album is the lead single "SexyBack", the style of which is described by Timberlake as "club funk".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VineyardMTVFunk_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-VineyardMTVFunk-10">[10]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the track "Damn Girl", which was produced by the Jawbreakers, incorporates '60s <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gospel_(music)" title="Gospel (music)">Gospel music</a> is infused in "Losing My Way", which is the only song in the album that features choir <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">arrangement</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyrics">Lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RickRubinSept09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="411" data-file-width="342" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RickRubinSept09.jpg/150px-RickRubinSept09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RickRubinSept09.jpg/225px-RickRubinSept09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RickRubinSept09.jpg/300px-RickRubinSept09.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RickRubinSept09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a> produced "(Another Song) All Over Again", the only song in the album that was written on paper.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the songs' lyrics were not written down on paper,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> as Timberlake believed it would only slow him down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moss_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Moss-7">[7]</a></sup> For most of the album's production, Timberlake composed the lyrics in his head and would record the song shortly after. Some songs were conceptualized within a relatively shorter time, while others took longer because Timberlake had wanted to incorporate variation. For instance, the lyrics to "Losing My Way" were in a narrative style which took Timberlake longer to write.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup> The only song that Timberlake wrote down on paper was the <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a>-produced "(Another Song) All Over Again". Rubin felt it was unusual for Timberlake because he requested the latter to write the lyrics first instead of recording it directly in the vocal booth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVineyard2007-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sharing common themes with <i>Justified</i>, <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> contains songs that are thematically based on and, according to Timberlake, were motivated by sex and love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> editor Jennifer Vineyard summarizes that the album illustrates "the very nature of how sex and love are interchangeable and immutable and contradictory and complementary all at once".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup> The first half of the album, <i>FutureSex</i>, generally focuses on themes about sex that are evident on songs like the title track "FutureSex/LoveSound", "LoveStoned", "Damn Girl" and "Sexy Ladies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup> The second half, <i>LoveSounds</i>, is the album's "sweet side",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup> encompassing songs such as "My Love", the <a href="/wiki/Slow_jam" title="Slow jam">slow jam</a> "Until the End of Time" and "What Goes Around... Comes Around". Meanwhile, "LoveStoned" transitions to the two-minute prelude "I Think She Knows".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although themes of sex and love are dominant in the album, the song "Losing My Way" diverges to a more serious topic, which was inspired by a <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary</a> of <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine" title="Methamphetamine">crystal meth</a> addiction that Timberlake watched.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup> Meanwhile, "(Another Song) All Over Again" is a homage to <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> musician <a href="/wiki/Donny_Hathaway" title="Donny Hathaway">Donny Hathaway</a>, according to Timberlake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup> The lyrics to "What Goes Around... Comes Around" are thought to have similar meaning to "Cry Me a River". In an interview, he revealed that the song was based on one of his friends' experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoss2_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoss2-14">[14]</a></sup> "My Love" was also noted as "arguably" similar with "Cry Me a River".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup> Timberlake however confirmed in many interviews that the record is not autobiographical, although he himself had an experience from which to draw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LongObserverSexy_15-7"><a href="#cite_note-LongObserverSexy-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vineyard3_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-Vineyard3-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Six major <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a> were issued from the album, led by "<a href="/wiki/SexyBack" title="SexyBack">SexyBack</a>" which was released on July 7, 2006, two months prior to the publication of the album. Regarding the song, Timberlake surmised he did not sound like he did before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeinerNYTLeading_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-WeinerNYTLeading-23">[23]</a></sup> "SexyBack", which lacks his distinctive <a href="/wiki/Falsetto" title="Falsetto">falsetto</a>, is seen as a complete departure from Timberlake's recognized sound,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20073_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20073-24">[24]</a></sup> and his management thought it might risk being unrecognizable as a "Justin Timberlake song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeinerNYTLeading_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-WeinerNYTLeading-23">[23]</a></sup> But that risk nonetheless appealed to Timberlake,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeinerNYTLeading_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-WeinerNYTLeading-23">[23]</a></sup> who reportedly insisted to have "SexyBack" released as the album's lead single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WeinerNYTLeading_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-WeinerNYTLeading-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> executive Barry Weiss, who initially doubted the suggestion, later told in an interview in February 2007 that albeit an "unusual record", it was a "risk that clearly paid off".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>"SexyBack" was followed with the release of "<a href="/wiki/My_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="My Love (Justin Timberlake song)">My Love</a>" in the third quarter of 2006, and "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_Around..._Comes_Around" title="What Goes Around... Comes Around">What Goes Around... Comes Around</a>" in early January 2007. The single releases for the standard edition of the album spanned a year, during which time the fourth single, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LoveStoned/I_Think_She_Knows" title="LoveStoned/I Think She Knows">LoveStoned/I Think She Knows</a>", was released. When the deluxe edition was issued, the duet version of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Until_the_End_of_Time_(Justin_Timberlake_and_Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles_song)" title="Until the End of Time (Justin Timberlake and Beyoncé Knowles song)">Until the End of Time</a>" was also released in the same month. The single version includes as its <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">B-side</a> the "Set the Mood (Prelude)", which is juxtaposed with "<a href="/wiki/Summer_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Summer Love (Justin Timberlake song)">Summer Love</a>" in the album's track listing. The European release of "Until the End of Time" omits "Set the Mood (Prelude)", and instead included "Summer Love" as double A-side.</p>
<p>Commercially, the album's first three singles have been the most successful in the domestic music market. They each peaked at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, giving Timberlake credit as the only artist to achieve such feat since R&amp;B singer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> accomplished four chart-topping singles between February and December 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> "SexyBack" and "My Love" have since been certified multi-platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), an achievement that was seen as "rare" amidst free file-sharing in the Internet, which had made reaching the million mark in sales a struggle in the music industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrownEWWants_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrownEWWants-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tour">Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jtstpaul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="643" data-file-width="542" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Jtstpaul.jpg/220px-Jtstpaul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Jtstpaul.jpg/330px-Jtstpaul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Jtstpaul.jpg/440px-Jtstpaul.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jtstpaul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Timberlake performing at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Paul,_Minnesota" title="St. Paul, Minnesota">St. Paul</a>, Minnesota, one of the venues of his first worldwide tour, the <a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveShow" title="FutureSex/LoveShow">FutureSex/LoveShow</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveShow" title="FutureSex/LoveShow">FutureSex/LoveShow</a></div>
<p>In support of the album, Timberlake embarked on the <a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveShow" title="FutureSex/LoveShow">FutureSex/LoveShow</a>, his first concert tour on a global scale. Promoted primarily by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AEG_Live" title="AEG Live">AEG Live</a>, the concert tour reached North America, Europe, Asia and Oceania, with 119 venues in total. It began on January 8, 2007, in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, California, and culminated in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, on December 6, 2007. FutureSex/LoveShow, which drew 1.6 million people worldwide, grossed a total of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Dollar" title="United States Dollar">US$</a>126.8 million, the third top-grossing concert tour in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, it was announced that Timberlake signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> network to broadcast the live concert. Timberlake had previously appeared on HBO, which aired the <a href="/wiki/No_Strings_Attached_Tour" title="No Strings Attached Tour">*NSYNC Live From Madison Square Garden</a> concert in 2000. FutureSex/LoveShow was taped on the second night at the <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> on August 16, 2007. The footage was broadcast by HBO on September 3, 2007, and later on September 6 due to demand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> On November 20, 2007, a two-disc edition of <i><a href="/wiki/FutureSex/LoveShow:_Live_from_Madison_Square_Garden" title="FutureSex/LoveShow: Live from Madison Square Garden">FutureSex/LoveShow: Live from Madison Square Garden</a></i> was released on DVD and Blu-ray formats that were sold exclusively by the retailer <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>. The release included extra footage including a song-by-song commentary by Timberlake and pre- and post-show clips.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, the broadcast earned Timberlake an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> in the category Outstanding Picture Editing For A Special (Single Or Multi-Camera).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> For Timberlake's performance of "What Goes Around... Comes Around" at the Madison Square Garden, Josh Tyrangiel of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine ranked it second on its list of top ten live performances in 2007. Tyrangiel writes, "It's a little on the long side, but Timberlake earns this symphonic take on What Goes Around from his HBO special."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On October 31, 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine announced the finalists for the 2007 <i>Billboard</i> Touring Awards, which was based on actual box office performance from January 1, 2007, to September 30, 2007. Timberlake was nominated in the categories Top Tour, Top Draw and Breakthrough Artist;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> he won the latter that was announced during the awards show on November 15, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> was released worldwide on September 13, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> More than a year after its initial release, a deluxe edition of the album was issued on November 27, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVStaff_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVStaff-36">[36]</a></sup> This edition contains three additional tracks on the album, each featuring guest artist. One of the tracks is a re-recording of "<a href="/wiki/Until_the_End_of_Time_(Justin_Timberlake_and_Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Until the End of Time (Justin Timberlake and Beyoncé song)">Until the End of Time</a>", now a duet between Timberlake and American R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>. Also included with the Deluxe Edition is a bonus DVD, which contains footage from Timberlake's live performances and behind the scenes on the music videos of four singles, including "SexyBack" and "What Goes Around... Comes Around". The main album included with the Deluxe Edition is the edited version; and an explicit version was not issued.</p>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine, Jive's mother company <a href="/wiki/Sony_BMG" title="Sony BMG">Sony BMG</a> offered 71 distinct products to tie in with <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>. This was an attempt at finding solutions to declining sales in physical albums, and Timberlake's album was among those offered in various configurations and versions. Aside from the album itself, the project included digital versions, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ringtones" title="Ringtones">ringtones</a>, wallpapers and individual tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before, an artist's release was made available in less than ten formats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BargfredeLaw_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-BargfredeLaw-38">[38]</a></sup> In recent years, however, versioning strategies have been increasingly applied to the recording industry. On the 2010 book <i>The Music Industry: Music in the Cloud</i> which examines such context, author Patrik Wikström noted <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> as one "high-profile" example.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wikstr.C3.B6mCloud_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wikstr.C3.B6mCloud-39">[39]</a></sup> From the project, a total of 115 versions or products have been sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BargfredeLaw_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-BargfredeLaw-38">[38]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a> (IFPI), the project has sold as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> more than 19 million units worldwide, 20 percent of which were sales on CD format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wikstr.C3.B6mCloud_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wikstr.C3.B6mCloud-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="3/5 stars"><img alt="3/5 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UncutReview_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-UncutReview-50">[50]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> was met with generally positive reviews from critics. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from mainstream publications, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 70, based on 25 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MC_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-MC-40">[40]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Torque_(magazine)" title="Torque (magazine)">Torque</a></i> commended Timberlake for "manag[ing] to surprise with an eclectic collection of sounds, and in a good way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Katy Kroll of <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> noted the album's sound as a "bit different, but the music's sex appeal remains a force to be reckoned with".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KrollBillboardRev_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-KrollBillboardRev-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> suggested that the album is not "an easy listen at first", but "repeated listening helps the tunes unravel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LATimesRev_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-LATimesRev-45">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> senior editor <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> commended Timberlake's "clear musical vision" and stated, "Graceless he may be, [he] is nevertheless kind of fascinating on <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ErlewineAllmusicRev_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-ErlewineAllmusicRev-41">[41]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i> called it a "set of forward-thinking pop reminiscent of" Prince's 1987 album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sign_%22O%22_the_Times" title='Sign "O" the Times'>Sign "O" the Times</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qmag_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Qmag-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kelefa_Sanneh" title="Kelefa Sanneh">Kelefa Sanneh</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> stated, "How well do Mr. Timberlake and Timbaland work together? So well that they can make even the world's most irritating percussion instrument, the human beatbox, sound pretty good."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SannehNYTRev_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-SannehNYTRev-53">[53]</a></sup> She also took notice of the album's preludes and interludes, writing, "Timbaland has long been known for hiding little surprises near the end of songs, and here he takes his obsession with transformation to new heights."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SannehNYTRev_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-SannehNYTRev-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a mixed review, <i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i> magazine found the album "laudable, but overreaching."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UncutReview_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-UncutReview-50">[50]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> felt that Timberlake and Timbaland's songwriting is "frustratingly awkward".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a>, writing for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, said that the album "almost works: close, but no enema."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PetridisGuardianRev_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-PetridisGuardianRev-44">[44]</a></sup> Ben Williams of <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine commented that Timberlake is "better at being sappy than sexy" and concluded, "If he hasn't yet invented a persona intriguing enough to live up to his music, give him credit for being one of the few white men still brave enough to make <a href="/wiki/African-American_music" title="African-American music">black music</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> found Timberlake's "best new" songs "thrilling", although "some of the up-tempo stuff flirts with mechanical muscle-flexing" and "Losing My Way" is a "well-meaning" but "clueless embarrassment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChristgauRSRev_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-ChristgauRSRev-49">[49]</a></sup> In his consumer guide for <a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a>, he cited "My Love" and "SexyBack" as highlights and gave the album a three-star honorable mention,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChristgauCG_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChristgauCG-56">[56]</a></sup> indicating "an enjoyable effort consumers attuned to its overriding aesthetic or individual vision may well treasure."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/49th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="49th Annual Grammy Awards">2007</a>, the album received four nominations at the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Pop Vocal Album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Timberlake lost the two; however, he won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a> for "SexyBack" and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> for "<a href="/wiki/My_Love_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="My Love (Justin Timberlake song)">My Love</a>", featuring rapper T.I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/50th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Annual Grammy Awards">following year</a> at the Grammys, "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_Around..._Comes_Around" title="What Goes Around... Comes Around">What Goes Around... Comes Around</a>" was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>; Timberlake won <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a> for the same song and another <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a> for "<a href="/wiki/LoveStoned" title="LoveStoned">LoveStoned/I Think She Knows (Interlude)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In 2007, Timberlake was nominated for seven categories at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2007 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, winning four, including Artist of the Year. He also earned the Quadruple Threat award, an accolade that recognizes those artists who have excelled in multiple media including music, fashion and acting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> For the album and its singles, Timberlake won World's Best Selling American Artist and World's Best Selling Pop Male Artist at the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Music_Awards" title="2007 World Music Awards">2007 World Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from procuring awards and nominations, the album earned numerous best-of lists in 2006<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20073_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20073-24">[24]</a></sup> and the following years. Music magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> listed <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> as their 26th among 2006's top 50 albums of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On the British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, the album made it at number 47 on the publication's list best 50 albums of 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On the general publication <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>, the album is ranked eighth among its list of ten best albums in 2006. The publication notes that Timberlake "levitates into a falsetto that honors Prince and Michael Jackson without stealing from them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> earned numerous best-of-the-decade lists. <i>Rolling Stone</i> ranked it 46th on their top 100 albums of the 2000s - calling it "an avant-garde sprawl of abstract electronica and hallucinatory space funk."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> ranked the album at number nine on their list of 10 best albums of the decade. It says that <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is an album that "redefined pop's cutting edge".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Earlier in 2008, the album made it at number 31 on the magazine's 100 new classics in music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The album received additional acclaim from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></i>, ranking the album at number 79 and 49 on their respective "Best of the 2000s" lists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> named it the greatest album of the 2000s and ranked it at 5 on their list of "The Greatest 50 Albums Since '93".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibelist_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-vibelist-73">[73]</a></sup> In 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> made a list of the 300 best albums of the past 30 years (1985-2014), raking the album at number 101.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Fueled by its lead single "SexyBack",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> sold more than 684,000 units in its first week, peaking at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, the official US albums chart. It became Timberlake's first number-one album as a solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The album has sold over four million units in the United States, and has been certified four-times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> became the eighteenth best-selling album of 2006 in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> As of March 2013, the album has sold 4.4 million copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ussales_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-ussales-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Internationally, the album was also well received, selling almost equal units and topping many charts worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20073_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20073-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCAUK_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-RCAUK-80">[80]</a></sup> Sony BMG distinguished <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> as the biggest-selling album among the record company's releases in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCAUK_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-RCAUK-80">[80]</a></sup> Weiss noted that in the past three to five years before the album's release, American artists found it increasingly hard to achieve commercial success in international music markets. He found that Timberlake was among those few "that successfully sells in every country around the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20071_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20071-19">[19]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>, the album has since sold more than 10 million units worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVEvolution_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVEvolution-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album debuted at number one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCAUK_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-RCAUK-80">[80]</a></sup> <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> became the biggest pre-order album in <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> history, breaking the all-time record for one week digital sales previously held by the English <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCAUK_80-3"><a href="#cite_note-RCAUK-80">[80]</a></sup> Elsewhere in Europe, the album debuted at number one in Ireland, and opened at number two in Sweden and Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.CE.B1Charts_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-.CE.B1Charts-82">[82]</a></sup> In Australia, the album peaked at number one and has since been certified five-times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a>, denoting shipments of over 350,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> was the thirty-fourth best-selling album of 2006 in Australia, and third in the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:28%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"It changed the game. A bold departure from the warm, synthesized soul that The Neptunes helmed on <i><a href="/wiki/Justified_(album)" title="Justified (album)">Justified</a></i>, <i>FutureSex</i> was steely and sweaty, a universal dance opus that made room for intimacy. The album had some of Timbaland's smartest work as a producer, with beds of elastic funk and electro-pop for Timberlake to roll around in. The album also had adult themes and f-bombs, speeding up the transition from Curly-Haired Boy to Shaved-Head Man for Timberlake. And it was so blindingly successful, from blockbuster sales to hit singles to a huge tour to real critical acclaim, that the pop world grew deeply anxious while awaiting Timberlake's post-<i>FutureSex</i> return, which finally occurred seven years later with <i><a href="/wiki/The_20/20_Experience" title="The 20/20 Experience">The 20/20 Experience</a></i>. And still, to me, those are not the greatest achievements of Timberlake's 2006 album. Ten years later, it's more clear than ever: <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> had the best first half of any pop album in 25 years. You have to go back to 1979 for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Off_the_Wall_(album)" title="Off the Wall (album)">Off The Wall</a></i>, by JT's idol <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, to find a pop album with a first half that matches up."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuse_TV" title="Fuse TV">Fuse TV</a>'s music critic Jason Lipshutz writing for the 10th anniversary of the release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuse_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-fuse-86">[86]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The success of <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> affected both Timberlake's and Timbaland's careers. For Timberlake, it further established his career as a solo artist. He comments, "'SexyBack' was the point when people stopped asking me when *NSYNC <sup>[<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]</sup> were going to reunite and started asking what I was going to do next."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Timberlake has also beefed up his fan base, gaining "hipster" fans in the wake of the album's success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Combining the international success of Timberlake's <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> and <a href="/wiki/Nelly_Furtado" title="Nelly Furtado">Nelly Furtado</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Loose_(Nelly_Furtado_album)" title="Loose (Nelly Furtado album)">Loose</a></i>, demands for Timbaland's work reportedly surged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrownEWWants_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-BrownEWWants-27">[27]</a></sup> Writing for <i>Entertainment Weekly</i>, Chris Willman remarked that <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> is "like Timberlake's '<a href="/wiki/Credibility" title="Credibility">cred</a>' record",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WillmanEWReview_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-WillmanEWReview-89">[89]</a></sup> although Chris Collis said Timbaland nearly stole the spotlight, sharing with Timberlake the "star" status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CollisEWRecord_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-CollisEWRecord-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from earning critical acclaim for the album, according to Sia Michel of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, Timberlake was responsible for popularizing in 2006 the catchphrase "I'm bringing sexy back",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollis20071_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollis20071-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MichelNYTCommit_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-MichelNYTCommit-91">[91]</a></sup> which is culled from the lead single "SexyBack". It spawned a "phenomenon" in which video-makers spoofed the song. At least four parodies gained attention such as "SweatyBack" and "HairyBack".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> In 2007, Timberlake is ranked among <i>Time</i> magazine's 100 men and women "whose power, talent or moral example is transforming the world". For the publication, Timbaland writes, "It's as if Justin had been born 26 years ago to deliver music to the world. There are those who follow and those who lead. Justin is a leader, setting the bar for what's expected of others."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The album has been added to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>'s musical library and archive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Maura Johnston from <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> called it an "ambitious classic", writing <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> "musically propelled the pop&amp;B genre with audio novellas, interlude twists, Timbaland's weirdo sound effects and that irresistible falsetto" and "embraced the hard/soft duality implied by the title to thrilling effect—and because of their mastery of that balancing act, <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i> would go on to influence, if not define, much of the pop music that came after it." also adding it "pushed boundaries more forcefully than works by fellow crooners R. Kelly and Usher."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibelist_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-vibelist-73">[73]</a></sup> For its 10th anniversary, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> editor Brittany Spanos wrote "Ten years ago, Timberlake destroyed any doubt of his artistry or potential with the mature, innovative <i>FutureSex/LoveSounds</i>. The pop star experimented with R&amp;B, funk and rock to create a piece of music well ahead of its time. Today, the LP's influence can still be heard in everything from the worldly electro-soul of <a href="/wiki/Zayn_Malik" title="Zayn Malik">Zayn Malik</a> to the moody sound of newcomers like <a href="/wiki/Bryson_Tiller" title="Bryson Tiller">Bryson Tiller</a>. The album also signaled Timberlake's transition from pop hitmaker and Hollywood It Boy to a legitimate force as a musician and actor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listing">Track listing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Track listing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Certifications">Certifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FutureSex/LoveSounds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Certifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col">Region</th>
<th scope="col">Certification</th>
